URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS728331794	2019-08-26 23:05:56	838	species	Crestless Curassow	Mitu tomentosum			1					Colombia	CO	Vaupés	CO-VAU							Curassow spot	L8905114	P	1.0179428	-70.0997916	2019-02-02	07:00:00	obsr22246	S54151865	Incidental	P20	EBIRD				2	0		0	1	1		with Edimilsa Lima.	This species to my knowledge has not been reported from this area previously, but the habitat in which we saw this bird seems consistent with other sites where it is well known. My local guide and I saw this bird cross the road at a distance of perhaps 15 m, well enough to see that the tip of the tail was dark or tawny, not pale. It had no white in the undertail coverts/crissum. The observation lasted perhaps 8 seconds. The guide indicated Crestless Curassow in her book. In researching this identification, I can't completely rule out a female Wattled Curassow from the views I had, but that species in not mapped near Mitú. Given the circumstances of the observation, I don't expect this report to be validated, but I didn't want to let the sighting go unreported, in case others are in this area. Probably unrelated, but the bird was moving in the same direction as a nearby troop of Common Wooly Monkeys, toward the north.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS1084219985	2021-08-05 03:28:58.02519	838	species	Crestless Curassow	Mitu tomentosum			1					Venezuela	VE	Amazonas	VE-Z							Junglaven (clausurado actualmente)	L7898784	H	5.1535800	-66.3118800	1991-02-27	06:00:00	obsr592701	S82478589	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	795	16.093		2	1	G6345735	0	1	0		We started with 2 Green Ibis flying along the Big Lagoon just after our 6:00 breakfast. We left with a guide at 6:40 to go by vehicle to the Rio Ventuari for a boat trip up the Ventuari to a tributary called Cano Guayage that gets cut off during low-water periods, trapping freshwater dolphins (Inia geoffrensis) within the lagoon. We set off in the boat at 7:30am, heading upriver on a cool, sunny morning. We we reached the mouth of the Rio Guayage at 8:15am. Recent rains had raised water level enough that it was no real problem getting the boat into the lagoon. The lower part of the river is fairly narrow, but as the waterway opened up, we had lovely views of a Crestless Curassow walking on open, sandy ground under the trees. We passed Sungrebes, Sunbitterns, Agami and Boat-billed Herons, and Green-and-rufous Kingfishers as we headed toward the upper end of the lagoon. We reached the upper end of the lagoon, where we could get out, at 9:50am. We watched the Amazonian River Dolphins feeding in the middle of the greatest expanse of water as we headed back. We reached the mouth of the tributary into the Ventuari at 11:10am and were back at the Camani dock at 11:40. Loaded and headed back at 11:50 and reached camp at 12:40pm. After a 1:00 lunch and some down time, we walked back out the road, birding 2:45-6:30pm, when our driver picked us up for the return to camp. We walked over to the edge of the Big Lagoon, where we had Spotted Puffbird and Band-tailed Nighthawks at dusk. Dinner was at 8:00pm.	We had a great view of one walking on open, sandy ground under the trees where the Cano Guayage opened up.
